  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47024509-26fb-4127-b027-0b459cead867'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer11189949456252513944">“I’ve left some clues for you.<br/>If you want them, turn the page.<br/>If you don’t, put the book back on the shelf, please.”<br/><br/>So begins the latest whirlwind romance from the bestselling authors of <i>Nick & Norah’s Infinite Playlist</i>.   <span id="freeText11189949456252513944" style="display:none">“I’ve left some clues for you.<br />If you want them, turn the page.<br />If you don’t, put the book back on the shelf, please.”<br /><br />So begins the latest whirlwind romance from the bestselling authors of <i>Nick &amp; Norah’s Infinite Playlist</i>. Lily has left a red notebook full of challenges on a favorite bookstore shelf, waiting for just the right guy to come along and accept its dares. But is Dash that right guy? Or are Dash and Lily only destined to trade dares, dreams, and desires in the notebook they pass back and forth at locations across New York? Could their in-person selves possibly connect as well as their notebook versions? Or will they be a comic mismatch of disastrous proportions?<br /><br />Rachel Cohn and David Levithan have written a love story that will have readers perusing bookstore shelves, looking and longing for a love (and a red notebook) of their own.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12242672292897767281">A solid 3 stars. I was completely enthralled in the beginning but as the pace of the story shifted, I severely lost interest. The setting and the characters and the plot complimented each other so well. I do wish the mystery of the notebook was preserved for longer during the story - I feel that is truly what this book had going for it, and it was completely lost when Dash and Lily had met. It is definitely a fun Christmas read, very "John Green-esque" and I did enjoy my time reading it. After h</span>
  <span id="freeText12242672292897767281" style="display:none">A solid 3 stars. I was completely enthralled in the beginning but as the pace of the story shifted, I severely lost interest. The setting and the characters and the plot complimented each other so well. I do wish the mystery of the notebook was preserved for longer during the story - I feel that is truly what this book had going for it, and it was completely lost when Dash and Lily had met. It is definitely a fun Christmas read, very "John Green-esque" and I did enjoy my time reading it. After hearing so many serious fans of this book be disappointed by the sequel, I don't think I'm interested enough to continue.</span>

Just show me in context with an interesting storyline (which it has), and strong characters (which it could have had.)</span>

<div id="review_2060715130" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060715130" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060715130?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060715130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14102760109608039737">3.5 stars. <br/><br/>Anyone up for a Christmas story in July? <br/><br/> This book put me in such a Holiday mood that I immediately downloaded the movie Almost Christmas on my computer upon starting it. <br/><br/>It wasn’t as good as this book. Rachel Cohn and David Levithan rock. Jingle all the way. I don’t know of a more curious and fitting writing pair. Or maybe I do, but I just can’t think of any right now. I’m still recuperating from the Christmas love. Ah, it hurts not to be in December right now. <br/><br/>Never you mind that. </span>
  <span id="freeText14102760109608039737" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br /><br />Anyone up for a Christmas story in July? <br /><br /> This book put me in such a Holiday mood that I immediately downloaded the movie Almost Christmas on my computer upon starting it. <br /><br />It wasn’t as good as this book. Rachel Cohn and David Levithan rock. Jingle all the way. I don’t know of a more curious and fitting writing pair. Or maybe I do, but I just can’t think of any right now. I’m still recuperating from the Christmas love. Ah, it hurts not to be in December right now. <br /><br />Never you mind that. No Canadian in their right mind would wish for winter to come. Back to the book—a book about books and dares and romances—it was quite charming. <br /><br />Dash and Lily do not know each other, but slowly they will. Dash finds a book leading to Lily if he dares and he does dare indeed. And so begins a series of unfortunate events for both characters.<br /><br />… Kidding. Sort of. Not all dares are elegant and not all dares are enchanting. A dare is a dare because it’s challenging and takes willingness. What will come out of it remains to be seen for you. <br /><br />This is a book about relationships—forming new ones and figuring existing ones out. Dash thought he was in love once, perhaps he was wrong. Lily never kissed a boy, perhaps this is her turn to smooch. <br /><br />Bleh, I feel old just saying that—smooch. Bleeeeeh. I might need to wash my mouth. <br /><br />So anyway, lovely book. A little unrealistic towards the end (why did you need to bring in the media, authors?) but otherwise a satisfying Christmas romance. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14102760109608039737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8426870756245282189">I really liked this!! I loved the characters and reading from their perspectives and how different they were. The premise and the plot and a lot of the quotes from this book were SO GREAT. <br/>My main hang up was that the two main characters used words and phrases that even I didn't know or wouldn't use and I am TWENTY FIVE.   <span id="freeText8426870756245282189" style="display:none">I really liked this!! I loved the characters and reading from their perspectives and how different they were. It didn't bother me enough to dislike this book, but there were a few times it was just a little too much. <br />BUT OVERALL GREAT IF YOU LIKE CONTEMP YOU WILL PROBABLY LIKE THIS.</span>

<div id="review_1763447564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763447564" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763447564?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763447564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9577261158539705862">Okay at first I didn't think I was going to like this book like I did Nick & Norah's Infinite Playlist but after I kept reading it <--- I was wrong! <br/><br/>I laughed so hard at certain parts that I almost peed myself! I really needed that today/tonight! No peeing myself but a great laugh. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474421975i/20596718.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Lily's parents leave her and her brother for the Christmas holidays, they go to Fiji. Their grandpa went off to Florida to see his girlfriend and Lily's brother is only interested in spending time with his boyfriend. </span>
  <span id="freeText9577261158539705862" style="display:none">Okay at first I didn't think I was going to like this book like I did Nick &amp; Norah's Infinite Playlist but after I kept reading it &lt;--- I was wrong! <br><br>I laughed so hard at certain parts that I almost peed myself! I really needed that today/tonight! No peeing myself but a great laugh. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474421975i/20596718.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lily's parents leave her and her brother for the Christmas holidays, they go to Fiji. Their grandpa went off to Florida to see his girlfriend and Lily's brother is only interested in spending time with his boyfriend. <br><br>So, Lily's brother Langston gives her the idea about the notebook. She fills this red notebook full of stuff and puts it in the bookstore in between some shelves hoping maybe someone would find it. And guess what? They did, Dash found the notebook and did his part of the dares, nothing too extreme and then he was supposed to leave the notebook in a place or with a person that Lily chose. <br><br>This went on through-out the story with them both giving each other things to do and then leave the notebook in weird places or with people they recruited. I thought it was so charming and cute. Some of the stuff was so hilarious and weird and I want to do it! :-) <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474421975ra/20596719.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love that these two lonely people happen to find each other at Christmas to do all of this craziness. It was sooooo much fun. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474421975ra/20596720.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At some point they do want to meet each other but some things go wrong and Dash has to run around and try to find Lily. She ran away and forgot to leave the notebook! So he has to go back to people that were involved and try to find her. He does eventually find her but it wasn't the greatest of times to find her so they part ways. <br><br>Then Lily sets out to find Dash, oh and Dash has this hilarious friend named Boomer that actually became friends with Lily before Dash did. There are other characters that are really cool in the book too and it seems some of them are on the couples side. <br><br>But oh the horror when Lily and Dash meet up again in person. Lily had just posted a sign where Dash lived and was on her way walking one of her dogs from her pet sitting and he was a bull mastiff. Lord have mercy, this is where I started . . . um . . . having pee moments and they kept going for quite some time. I thought I was going to crack a rib I was laughing so hard. <br><br><b>I need not have posted the sign, however. <br>Because five minutes after I posted it, Boris started loudly barking at a teenage boy who approached me as I scooped up the biggest piece of dog dung I'd ever seen. <br>"Lily?"<br>I looked up from my plastic bag filled with giant poo. <br>Of course. <br>It was Dash.<br>Who else would find me at this moment? First he found me drunk, now he found me cleaning up poo from a barking pony who was about to go into attack mode.</b><br><br>That's not even half of it, there's the ice skating with the dog (not by choice), flying giant poo, child killers (not really) and the save the flying baby tackle. Oh and the little bit of time in jail. <br><br>I freaking loved it. I love these authors. I want more of their books. Anything that makes me happy and almost, um, pee my pants - I want more of in my life. <br><br>Thank you and goodnight! ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/09/dash-lilys-book-of-dares-by-rachel.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_125287684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125287684" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125287684?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125287684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4008055268559936419">We had our first real snow this weekend and the advent season is approaching, so I decided to pick up <b>Dash & Lily's Book of Dares</b> to get in the mood for Christmas – at least a little bit. Actually, I wanted to save it for later in December, but my curiosity was simply too great.<br/><br/>It was a really sweet, but not too overly kitschy read featuring two likeable main characters. The spirit of the festive season came across in a great way and I enjoyed the dares passing between Lily and Dash with the hel</span>
  <span id="freeText4008055268559936419" style="display:none">We had our first real snow this weekend and the advent season is approaching, so I decided to pick up <b>Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</b> to get in the mood for Christmas – at least a little bit. Actually, I wanted to save it for later in December, but my curiosity was simply too great.<br /><br />It was a really sweet, but not too overly kitschy read featuring two likeable main characters. The spirit of the festive season came across in a great way and I enjoyed the dares passing between Lily and Dash with the help of a red notebook. Their story is probably not too realistic and would never happen in real life, but it was great to get lost in their almost fairytale-like romance for a few hours. If you are looking for a light and sweet read (that still has a little special touch) to get in the mood for Christmas and snow, I would recommend you give this book a try. It will not change your life or make a lasting expression with its message, but it's a lot of fun.<br /><br />The only thing that annoyed me: Dash and Lily come across as a little too sophisticated for my taste. The way they talk seems sometimes almost unrealistic for two teenagers. Also, they both love to read, and of course their love for books covers only the classics. In my opinion, you don't have to be a huge fan of the classics – and only the classics – to be allowed to call yourself a booklover.<br /><br />That being said, I nevertheless enjoyed <b>Dash and Lily's Book of Dares</b>, although I still like the other novel I read by Cohn and Leviathian, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25373.Nick___Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist" title="Nick &amp; Norah's Infinite Playlist by Rachel Cohn" rel="nofollow noopener">Nick &amp; Norah's Infinite Playlist</a>, a lot more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4008055268559936419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_174386824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174386824" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4404986-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299823285p2/4404986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174386824?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/4404986-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9305872-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4404986-maria?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4404986-maria?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4404986-maria?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174386824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5502429255631564504">I highly recommend <a href='http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/12/27/book-review-dash-lilys-book-of-dares-by-rachel-cohn-david-levithan/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dash & Lily's Book of Dares</a>.<br/><br/><b>DELIGHTFUL.</b><br/> <br/><i>Dash & Lily’s Book of Dares</i> is the perfect Christmas read. It took me around New York in the busiest time of the year with Dash’s abhorrence versus Lily’s ecstasy for the holidays. It kinda remind me of the movie Serendipity: same Christmas-in-New-York setting with the same non-meetings but with the longing of meeting the one another.<br/> <br/>Dash and Lily are the total opposites. Dash never recovered from his parents’ nasty divorce; Lily stayed</span>
  <span id="freeText5502429255631564504" style="display:none">I highly recommend <a href="http://bookchilla.wordpress.com/2011/12/27/book-review-dash-lilys-book-of-dares-by-rachel-cohn-david-levithan/" rel="nofollow noopener">Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</a>.<br /><br /><b>DELIGHTFUL.</b><br /> <br /><i>Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares</i> is the perfect Christmas read. It took me around New York in the busiest time of the year with Dash’s abhorrence versus Lily’s ecstasy for the holidays. It kinda remind me of the movie Serendipity: same Christmas-in-New-York setting with the same non-meetings but with the longing of meeting the one another.<br /> <br />Dash and Lily are the total opposites. Dash never recovered from his parents’ nasty divorce; Lily stayed at home while her parents celebrated their second honeymoon in Fiji. Dash reveled in being alone; Lily is scared of not having anybody. Dash is articulate; Lily is stumped on how to talk to boys (and girls!) her age. But they do have something in common – they love to read. and they wanted to believe that there is someone out there existing just for them. So cute.<br /> <br />I loved <b>Dash</b>‘s character more than Lily’s. His has a certain sadness and hope at the same time. I relished reading his POV because it’s very entertaining to see the switch of his train of thought from simple things to contemplative ones. I loved the scenes where (1) he’s feeling up Santa, (2) he’s being interrogated by Aunt Ida, and (3) he’s being lectured by Boomer, of all people. Dash is very charming in this unobtrusive way that makes being snarly so endearing.<br /> <br /><b>Lily</b> is the odd girl. Wearing her school uniform even during weekends with her worn chucks, she already accepted her eccentricity years ago. But after reading Dash’s writings in her notebook, she thought that maybe it’s time to get out of her family’s comfort and venture to a normal teenage life. I found it funny that she’s this dogwalker who also loves hanging out with her Grandpa’s friends but can give the middle finger on a whim.<br /> <br />Boomer, Aunt Ida, and Mark are secondary characters that made me laugh in more ways i thought possible. I love how they are solid and yet they do not overpower the main characters.<br /> <br /><i>Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares</i> is a story of what could be the machinings of first love set in snow-capped New York. Dash &amp; Lily’s mismatches left me light-hearted and hopeful. I just felt good after reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5502429255631564504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_208713098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208713098" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208713098?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375859557" href="/book/show/10264464-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-after-university">read-after-university</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208713098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1192228081223991265">I was looking for some young adult Christmas books to read over the holidays and I chose <i>Dash & Lily’s Book of Dares</i> & <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3213286.Let_It_Snow_Three_Holiday_Romances' title='Let It Snow Three Holiday Romances by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Let It Snow</a>
</i>. I thought <i>Dash & Lily</i> was going to be a cute, Christmas read and nothing more. I didn’t expect it to be so witty and ingenious. I loved Dash straight away. Some people will certainly find him obnoxious at first (he’ll quite happily refer to himself as erudite and bookish), but I love a guy who’s articulate without being pretentious. We’re introduced to Dash firs</span>
  <span id="freeText1192228081223991265" style="display:none">I was looking for some young adult Christmas books to read over the holidays and I chose <i>Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares</i> &amp; <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3213286.Let_It_Snow_Three_Holiday_Romances" title="Let It Snow Three Holiday Romances by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Let It Snow</a>
</i>. I thought <i>Dash &amp; Lily</i> was going to be a cute, Christmas read and nothing more. I didn’t expect it to be so witty and ingenious. I loved Dash straight away. Some people will certainly find him obnoxious at first (he’ll quite happily refer to himself as erudite and bookish), but I love a guy who’s articulate without being pretentious. We’re introduced to Dash first as he discovers Lily’s red moleskin notebook, instructing him to find a book on French Pianism. And this (wonderful, brilliant idea) sends him on a journey where impulsiveness is a requirement.<br /><br /><i>Dash &amp; Lily</i> is one of those books that made me want to go on an adventure. I wanted to pack my bags and head to NYC, bake Lebkuchen spice cookies, and spend all day in The Strand bookshop. It’s one of those books that reminded me that while spending all day reading is a wonderful thing, I didn’t want to be one of those people that envies the lives of fictional characters. If I wanted to be eating a chocolate pizza at Max Brenner (actually, I’d choose The S’mores Concoction) then I bloody well needed to go out there and do it! However, even if <i>Dash &amp; Lily</i> doesn’t persuade you to make life changing decisions, you’ll still love both Dash and Lily and the myriad of eccentric characters that you’ll come across. It’s hilarious to the point where it actually made me laugh out loud, rather than just smile. I particularly enjoyed Dash’s quick-witted banter about tea with Lily’s aunt.<br /><br />So, <i>Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares</i> is definitely one of my favourite books of 2011. I’d suggest running to the nearest bookshop (specifically, The Strand, if you’re able to) and buying it straight away! Don’t wait until Christmas 2012.<br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1192228081223991265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1844725471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1844725471" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1844725471?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9305872-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=nyc">nyc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1844725471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8031090935858307496"><br/><i>- Dash – December 21st Imagine this: You’re in your favorite bookstore, scanning the shelves. You get to the section where a favorite author’s books reside, and there, nestled in comfortably between the incredibly familiar spines, sits a red notebook. What do you do? The choice, I think, is obvious: You take down the red notebook and open it.</i><br/><br/>When Dash opens the cover he finds a note on the first page.<br/><br/><i>I’ve left some clues for you.<br/>If you want them, turn the page.<br/>If you don’t, put the book back on </i></span>
  <span id="freeText8031090935858307496" style="display:none"><br /><i>- Dash – December 21st Imagine this: You’re in your favorite bookstore, scanning the shelves. You get to the section where a favorite author’s books reside, and there, nestled in comfortably between the incredibly familiar spines, sits a red notebook. What do you do? The choice, I think, is obvious: You take down the red notebook and open it.</i><br /><br />When Dash opens the cover he finds a note on the first page.<br /><br /><i>I’ve left some clues for you.<br />If you want them, turn the page.<br />If you don’t, put the book back on the shelf, please.</i><br /><br />There are more instructions leading him to other books with other instructions. <br /><br />He follows all the leads, makes his notes, and waits. <br /><br />The red notebook becomes their only means of communication, and over a relatively short period of time they begin to share a little bit of themselves with the other. Christmas memories. Christmas “Wish List” items. His – an Unabridged Oxford English Dictionary, all 20 volumes. <br /><br />Rachel Cohn and David Leviathan have written a relatively short, sweet, and fun novel about young love looked at from both sides using alternating chapters – his and hers – Dash’s and Lily’s views. Romance-Light for the YA crowd, maybe especially for those who consider themselves “bookish”. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8031090935858307496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText14555733948178411130" style="display:none">Before you start throwing things at me, remember the Christmas spirit.<br /><br /> I know everybody loves this book and thinks Lily &amp; Dash are #Goals! but Nah! <br /><br />This book was so boring I had to force myself to finish it. I expected this to be cute and sweet little holiday romance but I just did not enjoy this book. Lily and Dash have ZERO chemistry and I just kind of skimmed the last 20 pages. Lily was not an enjoyable character for me. She behaved like a 10 year old but got mad when people treated her like a 10 year old. <br /><br />I'm obviously in the minority so I'm not going to give a recommendation. Not every book is meant for every reader. <br /><br />Happy Holidays Everybody!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6476128391389788025">TBR Reduce Challenge #22- 2011 (Stefanie) <br/><br/>I got a few strange, even evil, looks after explaining I was reading a Christmas book in spring. Like I'm daring the winter weather to come back to Canada and piss everyone off. But, I didn't really care since this book was an absolute hoot!<br/><br/>I really don't have to much to say about this book, except It was freaken hilarious and I don't think I've had so much fun reading about two characters who don't even meet till almost the end of the book, but never th</span>
  <span id="freeText6476128391389788025" style="display:none">TBR Reduce Challenge #22- 2011 (Stefanie) <br /><br />I got a few strange, even evil, looks after explaining I was reading a Christmas book in spring. Like I'm daring the winter weather to come back to Canada and piss everyone off. But, I didn't really care since this book was an absolute hoot!<br /><br />I really don't have to much to say about this book, except It was freaken hilarious and I don't think I've had so much fun reading about two characters who don't even meet till almost the end of the book, but never the less, Dash and Lily are quite the amusing couple. Intelligent, snarky and very daring. It was fun seeing where these two will take each other, and the reader next, not to mention what they made each other do. Hats off to the other secondary characters, all of them and I mean <i>all</i> of them seemed to add that extra blast to the plot. Loved the writing! It was the perfect pace for a fun filled adventure around the streets of NY.<br />Bottom line, <b>Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</b> was a really fun read. It made me laugh out loud and smile a stupid smile and it was even worth the weird death stares. Loved it!<br /><br /><br />Some of my favorite quotes/moments (There are tons, so these are just a few)<br /><br />~"It looks like Animal and Miss Piggy had sex, and this was the spawn"<br /><br />~Feeling up Santa (LOL!)<br /><br />~The Secret tactic of a good hard bargainer is know when to compromise.<br />For instance.<br />I will demand a puppy if I am forced to move to Fiji.<br />But I will settle for a bunny.<br /><br />~"I was just trying to imagine a situation where one person would need twelve umbrellas. It seems almost indecent to have so many, when there are so many people who don't have any."<br /><br />~"With all due respect, if you’re forty three, then I’m a fetus." <br /><br />~"Because you know how a cow chews grass? And he or she chews and chews and chews? Well, green tea tastes like French-kissing that cow after it’s done chewing all that grass." <br /><br />...and basically the whole Q&amp;A between grandma and Dash;)<br /><br />Fun stuff! Great book! Read it!</span>

        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-for-high-school-book-club">read-for-high-school-book-club</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156237340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14012112557508655517">This book was cute and funny, but failed to make me care about the actual characters as opposed to the things happening to them.<br/><br/>I liked the premise. Two unusual individuals communicate through a moleskin notebook and kindle an awkward romance - but meeting in real life brings a myriad of difficulties they never imagined. There were so many interesting ideas in this book: Can love really bloom from interactions not taking place in real life? Should one should wait for love to come to them or acti</span>
  <span id="freeText14012112557508655517" style="display:none">This book was cute and funny, but failed to make me care about the actual characters as opposed to the things happening to them.<br /><br />I liked the premise. Two unusual individuals communicate through a moleskin notebook and kindle an awkward romance - but meeting in real life brings a myriad of difficulties they never imagined. There were so many interesting ideas in this book: Can love really bloom from interactions not taking place in real life? Should one should wait for love to come to them or actively pursue it? And what is love, to be exact?<br /><br />The flaw that presented itself was the development of these themes - they could have been deep and introspective, but seemed shoddy and stale. Neither Dash or Lily grabbed my heart, and I could barely connect to them through all the random events taking place (for example, when Dash is attacked with snowballs by little kids while carrying a bag of yogurt).<br /><br />Books from these two authors may not be my thing, but fans of David Levithan and Rachel Cohn's previous works will probably enjoy <i>Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</i>.<br /><br />Want to read more of my writing? Follow me <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1824170135" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4870208667582165152">What began as a literary treasure hunt flirtation between a couple of cute kids quickly became...<br/><br/>A truly delightful and innocent romance. :) <br/><br/><br/><br/>Believe me, no one is more shocked than me how much I fell into and loved this little book. I mean, it wasn't just the literary side or the well-spoken Snarl or the impulsive Lily. It was the entire shape of the novel with all of the normal conventions: the shy flirtations, the near misses, the almost-meetings, and then, most dangerously, the other boys and</span>
  <span id="freeText4870208667582165152" style="display:none">What began as a literary treasure hunt flirtation between a couple of cute kids quickly became...<br /><br />A truly delightful and innocent romance. :) <br /><br /><br /><br />Believe me, no one is more shocked than me how much I fell into and loved this little book. I mean, it wasn't just the literary side or the well-spoken Snarl or the impulsive Lily. It was the entire shape of the novel with all of the normal conventions: the shy flirtations, the near misses, the almost-meetings, and then, most dangerously, the other boys and girls. It was all delightful and sooooo innocent. :) Even the Crimson Alert and the Sweaty Santa, it evokes a different sensation in adults, still managed to come across as INNOCENT on the page.<br /><br />And I liked it. I really really liked it.<br /><br />It's like opening a door to an alternate dimension and discovering that everything is gentle and loyal and honorable and smart. *shiver* It's so odd! And pretty! :)<br /><br />And of course, the writing is also quite beautiful, too. And charming. :)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6220531114822949997"><b>Rating Clarification: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I loved this book. A.L.O.T.!! And all I can chalk it up to is the fact that I needed a good laugh. I downright, gut wrenching good laugh and this book did it. I literally laughed so much throughout the story that I’d stop and read passages to whatever family member was in listening distance because to me… it was comic brilliance. That is the true markings of a funny book IMO, when my family yells in surrender, “Enough! We know you’ve lost your mind!” <br/><br/>The dares were</span>
  <span id="freeText6220531114822949997" style="display:none"><b>Rating Clarification: 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I loved this book. A.L.O.T.!! And all I can chalk it up to is the fact that I needed a good laugh. I downright, gut wrenching good laugh and this book did it. I literally laughed so much throughout the story that I’d stop and read passages to whatever family member was in listening distance because to me… it was comic brilliance. That is the true markings of a funny book IMO, when my family yells in surrender, “Enough! We know you’ve lost your mind!” <br /><br />The dares were fun and exciting and the characters that made up this story warmed my heart. Their epistolary flirtation was continuously captivating and I didn’t want the red notebook journey to end. I wish I would have had the nerve to pull off a stunt like that when I was a teenager. What a hoot!<br /><br />Dash is the king of hilarious!! I want to possess his snark. He is my snark hero. *applauds* His snarly, pensive, yet caring character was worthy of a fictional crush. <br /><br /><b>Favorite Dash lines:</b><br /><i>I’m looking for ‘Fat Hoochie Prom Queen.’ No response. It’s a BOOK, not a person.<br /><br />Hello, my name ees Lebkuchen Spice, and I vant to show you my coooooookies….<br /><br />It looks like Animal and Miss Piggy had sex, and this was the spawn.<br /><br />Ex-squeamish me?!<br /><br />With all due respect, if you’re forty three, then I’m a fetus.<br /><br />Because you know how a cow chews grass? And he or she chews and chews and chews? Well, green tea tastes like French-kissing that cow after it’s done chewing all that grass.</i><br /><br />LMAO!<br /><br />Lily is quirky and funny as hell! Props to her for giving it one more try after her epic, embarrassing debut to Dash. I loved her style and come on! I’m a sucker for animal lovers. My kind of girl… no doubt.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Lily lines:</b><br /><i>Do you speak Catalan? ‘No’ Lily responded. I said no in Catalan, but since the word sounds the same in English, Hermione didn’t notice.<br /><br />I had my two favorite dogs with me in the park – Lola and Dude, a little pug-Chi mix and a giant chocolate Lab. It’s true love between them. You can tell by how eagerly they sniff each other’s ….<br /><br />“Okay!” Lilly screeched. “Let’s go upstairs! I love books about freaks.” Because I am one. You might be too. Let’s be freaks together?<br /><br />Snap. Crackly. Dash yum. Ouch. Cursing – not so dashing.</i><br /><br />Great book that’s a perfect read for the Christmas holidays! Don't make me dare you to read it... :P</span>
  <a data-text-id="6220531114822949997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_249249515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/249249515" />
    <a title="Taneika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika"><img alt="Taneika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564410672p2/5591031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/249249515?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taneika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taneika" href="/user/show/5591031-taneika">Taneika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781742374666" href="/book/show/9649873-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer249249515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11029507379477168200"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href='http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ ' rel='nofollow noopener'>Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br/><br/>What can I say about this? Oh, I have such a hard time writing reviews for contemporary books (Brodie, I know what you're going to say, but I won't say this review is dodgy... for your sake), I just don't find them as easy to review as fantasy or paranormal because not only have I only just started reading contemporary, but most of the time, I feel I can seriously relate in one way or the other.<br/><br/>A snarly boy named Dash finds a red mole</span>
  <span id="freeText11029507379477168200" style="display:none"><b>More of my reviews can be found at <a href="http://flippingthroughthepages00.blogspot.com/ " rel="nofollow noopener">Flipping Through the Pages</a>!</b><br /><br />What can I say about this? Oh, I have such a hard time writing reviews for contemporary books (Brodie, I know what you're going to say, but I won't say this review is dodgy... for your sake), I just don't find them as easy to review as fantasy or paranormal because not only have I only just started reading contemporary, but most of the time, I feel I can seriously relate in one way or the other.<br /><br />A snarly boy named Dash finds a red moleskine notebook right next to his favourite author's books in The Strand*, this notebook has been written by the sensible and quirky Lily. In the notebook, Lily has written clues, but instead of putting the notebook back on the shelf, Dash takes the notebook and starts his own game with Lily. The result is hilarious!<br /><br />The book is told by both Dash and Lily's perspective and I loved how distinct and fresh both of their personalities were. I was a bit worried as to how this would turn out as it's written by two authors, but they've managed to have the same voice and writing style whilst setting their character's apart from eachother. <br /><br />The setting - Christmas in New York. OH, HOW CLICHE' you say! (Would you look at that, I'm a poet!) No, this is perfect as we have Dash who can't stand Christmas and couldn't care less, and we have Lily who is to say the least, <b>obsessed</b> with Christmas. It's really great though, because Christmas Day isn't even that much of a big deal in this book. It's the lead up to Christmas that is hilarious and what makes each of the character's personalities shine through (like freakishly busy department stores and seeing Santa) and what happens to the character's after Christmas that makes you love these two.<br /><br />The minor characters are great and again, have completely distinct personalities. BOOMER! Hahahaha! I love Boomer! And how <b>over enthused</b> he is about everything! Every bit of dialogue from Boomer has an explanation point! What was great, was that whilst it was always "!", it still didn't feel overdone or stupid!<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a really cute, fun read and it was perfect because whilst I haven't been reading much in the past two weeks (believe me, I'd rather be reading!), this kept me occupied and made me smile so much :)<br />I'll leave you with a few quotes I loved...<br /><br /><i>"We all just took the bookstore at its word, because if you couldn't trust a bookstore, who could you trust?".</i><br />So true, Dash. So true.<br /><br /><i>"Dear man, you are a genius. I'm so glad my father forced me to marry you and allow you to impregnate me every year."</i><br />Oh, Lily, your comments about these sorts of things make me laugh and don't come across as if the author is trying to shove her beliefs down your throat. Plus, from what I could understand, I'm generally on the side of the author!<br /><br /><i>"I expected Sherlock Holmes and Jane Austin to be thumb wrestling in the corner."</i><br />HAHA! The visual I got from this sentence was incredible, and sorta weird...<br /><br /><br />*I googled The Strand and died a little inside. I am now making it my personal goal to not only travel the world, but to go to New York and spend hours browsing the shelves at The Strand and to bask in it's greatness. I don't know if it's true, but it apparently has 18 miles (28km for those who, like me, don't understand miles, lbs etcetc) worth of books. 28000m worth of bookish pleasure. *starts daydreaming*.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11029507379477168200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_463723826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463723826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer91268793554824411"><b>Video duology review (spoiler free)-</b> <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/GMrMYuM5_k4'>https://youtu.be/GMrMYuM5_k4</a><br/><br/>I love, love, loved the premise of this book - that two people communicate through a notebook that they leave around the city for each other to find. And the portion of this book where Dash and Lily's relationship was confined to the notebook probably earned 5 stars from me. However, I started to lose interest once they met in person. Not because they met, I still thought they were their charming selves, but there was a scene that </span>
  <span id="freeText91268793554824411" style="display:none"><b>Video duology review (spoiler free)-</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/GMrMYuM5_k4">https://youtu.be/GMrMYuM5_k4</a><br /><br />I love, love, loved the premise of this book - that two people communicate through a notebook that they leave around the city for each other to find. And the portion of this book where Dash and Lily's relationship was confined to the notebook probably earned 5 stars from me. However, I started to lose interest once they met in person. Not because they met, I still thought they were their charming selves, but there was a scene that seemed SO whacky that I couldn't understand why this was added to the plot. It was just a little too silly for me, it didn't sit well in the tone of the rest of the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The scene I'm talking about is Dash and Lily's second meeting in the park when the dog gets away and Lily saves a baby but a whole fuss is made about them being baby snatchers. I didn't think this chaos moved along the story or the relationship of D and L. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The other thing I really didn't like was the ending. You know, I think that there is a way to end a book at the beginning of a scene and still impart a sense of closure to it, but this book did not do that. I felt like I was cut off mid sentence. It was like, oh hey there aren't any pages left so we'd better just wrap this up. It felt sloppy to me. It didn't feel like an ending. There was no sense of closure, and leading up to it there was no sense of urgency that we were reaching any kind of resolution. I mean, I feel like where they ended it was a good stopping place, it just didn't have the correct words and feeling to satisfy me. So, a star gets lost, sorry.<br /><br />I believe this book covers the dates Dec 21st through Jan 1st. I actually started reading it on Dec 21st (not planned) so it was a neat experience to read about the characters on the same day. If that makes sense? Anyway, just thought I would let anyone know who is like me and can only tolerate Christmas theme books at Christmas time.</span>

<div id="review_403736089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/403736089" />
    <a title="Veronique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12371602-veronique"><img alt="Veronique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590509341p2/12371602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/403736089?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronique" href="/user/show/12371602-veronique">Veronique</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2015">r2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2016">r2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12371602-veronique?shelf=r2019">r2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403736089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8326653948202962397">Re-read<br/><br/><i>“But isn't this a dance? Isn't all of this a dance? Isn't that what we do with words? Isn't that what we do when we talk, when we spar, when we make plans or leave it to chance? Some of it's choreographed. Some of the steps have been done for ages. And the rest -- the rest is spontaneous. The rest has to be decided on the floor, in the moment, before the music ends.” </i><br/><br/>Somehow, every year since 2011, around Christmas, I end up re-reading <i>Dash and Lily's Book of Dares</i>. It isn't a literary cl</span>
  <span id="freeText8326653948202962397" style="display:none">Re-read<br /><br /><i>“But isn't this a dance? Isn't all of this a dance? Isn't that what we do with words? Isn't that what we do when we talk, when we spar, when we make plans or leave it to chance? Some of it's choreographed. Some of the steps have been done for ages. And the rest -- the rest is spontaneous. The rest has to be decided on the floor, in the moment, before the music ends.” </i><br /><br />Somehow, every year since 2011, around Christmas, I end up re-reading <i>Dash and Lily's Book of Dares</i>. It isn't a literary classic but somehow this book talks to me, combining colourful characters, brilliant dialogue, hilarious situations, New York during the festive season, all tied up as a light YA romance with a heavy literary taste.<br /><br /><i>“I was horribly bookish, to the point of coming right out and saying it, which I knew was not socially acceptable. I particularly loved the adjective bookish, which I found other people used about as often as ramrod or chum or teetotaler.”<br /><br />“It looks like Animal and Miss piggy had sex," I said. "And this was the spawn." <br />"My eyes!" Boomer cried. "My eyes! I can't stop seeing it now that you've said it!” </i><br /><br />The idea of leaving a notebook with clues in a bookshop to find a kindred spirit is just spot on for a book lover like me. Dash and Lily 'meet' through this medium and share messages and stories while compelling each other to seek out the notebook from hiding places around the city. At first, the deliciously crafted dares spur the characters on, but soon the messages become much more important. Both end up expressing their beliefs and feelings, allowing them to be more truthfull and open than if they'd met face to face, with positive and negative consequences.<br /><br /><i>“Be careful what you’re doing, because no one is ever who you want them to be. And the less you really know them, the more likely you are to confuse them with the girl or boy in your head” </i><br /><br />This witty and quirky story is just the ticket to get you in the mood for Christmas.<br /><br />PS: Yes, when I visited New York, I just had to go to The Strand and have a look... :O)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8326653948202962397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer493609275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5370275565058710022">Dash & Lily's Book of Dares was a ton of fun to read. I can see why it garnered so many prizes and awards. It's fantastically written by this quirky duet who is Rachel Cohn and David Levithan.<br/><br/>The story starts with Dash finding a red Moleskine diary hidden among other books on the shelves of a renowned NY bookshop, The Strand. On its pages, instructions for a dare by a mysterious girl. Dash, an incredibly bookish and snarly 16 years old with a love for the word fanciful, accepts the dare and star</span>
  <span id="freeText5370275565058710022" style="display:none">Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares was a ton of fun to read. I can see why it garnered so many prizes and awards. It's fantastically written by this quirky duet who is Rachel Cohn and David Levithan.<br /><br />The story starts with Dash finding a red Moleskine diary hidden among other books on the shelves of a renowned NY bookshop, The Strand. On its pages, instructions for a dare by a mysterious girl. Dash, an incredibly bookish and snarly 16 years old with a love for the word fanciful, accepts the dare and starts a series of events, one more hilarious than the other, which will bring the two teens to chase each other around New York City in a sort of comedy of errors. <br /><br />There are so many scenes I laughed out loud at, it's difficult to count them. The cast of characters is unique: great Aunt Ida and Boomer star among the others but I couldn't really point out an uninteresting character if I wanted to.<br />The only complaint that I have about this book is that the situations and the people are so much larger than life that they become almost unbelievable. To say eccentric is probably an understatement. These kids, Dash and Lily, are so unbelievably erudite and bookish that I feel like a dimwit when reading their dialogues. And if I feel like a dimwit at the venerable age of 36, what is a proper teenager going to feel? Spurred to read more?<br />They're just too mature, too profound, so much so that end in end, you can just see they come out of the pens of two adult, smart writers. <br /><br />Nonetheless, I think I liked this even more that Nick &amp; Norah's Infinite Playlist. A fun, fun read I definitely recommend.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5370275565058710022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_453128696" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453128696" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453128696?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848451728" href="/book/show/16051601-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453128696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9656495975405651613">Dash and Lily’s Book of Dares is a wacky romp through New York, starting in the famous book store, The Strand. It had me laughing hysterically in parts, and is laced with heartfelt introspection. <br/><br/>The story starts out with a red notebook and a dare. This notebook lands into the hands of Dash, the perfect person for this pursuit. It’s Christmas time and Dash is alone by his own design. He’s not a big fan of Christmas, and some of the assignments or dares are pure torture for him because of this. T</span>
  <span id="freeText9656495975405651613" style="display:none">Dash and Lily’s Book of Dares is a wacky romp through New York, starting in the famous book store, The Strand. It had me laughing hysterically in parts, and is laced with heartfelt introspection. <br /><br />The story starts out with a red notebook and a dare. This notebook lands into the hands of Dash, the perfect person for this pursuit. It’s Christmas time and Dash is alone by his own design. He’s not a big fan of Christmas, and some of the assignments or dares are pure torture for him because of this. This is a testament to how invested he is in these dares and in finding out who’s at the bottom of them. <br /><br />Lily is the author of the red notebook. She’s a little bizarre and doesn’t quite fit in, and doesn’t have any close girlfriends. Instead she’s close to her family. At the urging of her brother, she sets up the red notebook for the perfect person to find at the bookstore she loves. Lily has exactly the opposite view of Christmas from Dash, she absolutely loves everything about it, but this year she’s on her own since her parents went to Fiji and her grandfather went to Florida. Her brother is in town but he’s caught up in a new intense romance and can’t be bothered to entertain Lily, she’s bored and alone, so Dash’s counter dares couldn’t have happened at a more perfect time. <br /><br />This story was co-written by David Levithan and Rachel Cohn and chapters were passed back and forth, each of them writing in response to the others writing. I recently met these two at an author signing and it was evident from their interaction they have an easy and fun relationship, and this definitely translates into the writing. Their banter back and forth in person was just as witty and hilarious as it is in the book. At one point while reading this, I was cracking up so hard I was crying. This scene may or may not have included: a large dog, angry mothers, baby catching, a crimson alert, and the police. Wacky, slap-stick humor at its best! <br /><br />For those of you like me who require romance in a story, fear not! These two, in spite of their differences, seem to connect so well without even meeting each other at first. I guess we can thank Rachel Cohn for the romance, because she’s the one who pushed for a romantic and happy ending that’ll put a smile on your face. David was going to be so cruel!! <br /><br /><i>A copy was provided by Mira Ink through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you! </i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9656495975405651613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060962861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11841541453932312471">Since it is Christmas time it is only proper for me to review a book based on this time of the year. <br/><br/>I am not a big fan of Christmas, mostly because I grew up celebrating the Three Kings’ Day celebration (which is actually really fun, and everyone should celebrate), but also because I am not a big fan of Christmas songs, or films, or the dress code. To me it seems pointless, and the songs give me headaches, and I do not like romance as much. But I do love the family aspect and all that, I am not</span>
  <span id="freeText11841541453932312471" style="display:none">Since it is Christmas time it is only proper for me to review a book based on this time of the year. <br><br>I am not a big fan of Christmas, mostly because I grew up celebrating the Three Kings’ Day celebration (which is actually really fun, and everyone should celebrate), but also because I am not a big fan of Christmas songs, or films, or the dress code. To me it seems pointless, and the songs give me headaches, and I do not like romance as much. But I do love the family aspect and all that, I am not a total Grinch. So for the longest time I blamed my lack of affection for the holiday as the reason I did not enjoy this book at all, now I realize it is not my fault, but the book is truly horrid (sorry Torie and all my friends that loved it, but I am not really sorry, because I hate it).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450800219ra/17470918.gif" width="415" height="212" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It follows Dash and Lily as they sent each other clues via books. Interesting story right? Well yes, but poorly developed.<br><br>It was not a good book, simply was not. <b>The characters were the biggest issue.</b><br><br><b>Dash:</b> a misanthropic boy, as in dislikes humanity. It is not like he picked up Moliere, Swift, or Plato and saw their reasoning and decided being misanthropic made sense for him, nah, he is just like that with no actually good motive. I mean, this kid compares himself to a Bolshevik. I do not think he has ever in his life read what a Bolshevik is, and is just trying to sound cool, which he fails. I am not going to attack the way he speaks, because I talk like that to my friends most of the time, because I am like that, however, his voice really did not suit him. Not because he is a teen and it is smart talk, but because I cannot actually believe Dash is clever at all. One of the instances he tries to be is this one: <i> “ “Happy Hanukkah,” I said. Because I always liked to say the wrong holiday, just to see how the other person would react.” </i>As if another person’s religious holiday should be a funny thing. Let us just go around and test everyone on what they believe in, and if they pick up on it and try to explain to us that they go by another holiday, then they must be horrid people, when in reality, Dash is the horrid one. You are not Augustus Waters at all sir, nope, nope, and nope.<br><br><b>Lily: </b>Nah, she is not my type of character at all. Not because I am a Grinch and she loves Christmas, but because she had no depth at all. I do not think she was superficial, she did seem to love Christmas and all that, but she seemed like a cut out carbon copy of one of those romantic comedies where the girl’s sole purpose is to be there for the bettering of the man character, not a manic pixie dream girl, but something along those lines. The big peeve though was how shallow she actually is. Throughput most of the book, as she is figuring out all of the clues, she keeps hoping the guy is cute and not ugly. She also then goes on to offend <b>Hermione Granger </b>from Harry Potter: <i>“ I’ve always resented Hermione, because I wanted to be her so badly and she never seemed to appreciate as much as I thought she should that she got to be her. She got to live at Hogwarts be friends with Harry and kiss Ron, which was supposed to happen to me.”</i> Excuse you! What the hell is this? What did she want Hermione to do? Act like a stereotypical muggle-born? Being constantly grateful for her skills instead of being cool about it like everyone else? Crawl through the floor and wipe the boots of prejudiced purebloods with her tongue as thank you? I am terrified that people like her exist.<br>And it is not as if the writing was so brilliant that I could ignore these imbeciles. No, it was bellow average. Look I love John Green’s writing, he writes smart characters with smart mouths that remind me of myself, but this book took all of the “intelligent talk” and gave it to a pretentious little possum that seemed to never have actually heard of any of these things in the correct context and just used them without having any knowledge of what they were.<br><br><b>The only thing in this book that made some sense was this:<i></i></b> “You think fairy tales are only for girls? Here’s a hint -<b> ask yourself who wrote them</b>. I assure you, it wasn’t just the women.<b> It’s the great male fantasy </b>- all it takes is one dance to know that she’s the one. All it takes is the sound of her song from the tower, or a look at her sleeping face. And right away you know - this is the girl in your head, sleeping or dancing or singing in front of you. Yes, girls want their princes, but boys want their princesses just as much. And they don’t want a very long courtships. They want to know immediately.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="11841541453932312471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
