<div id="review_1763973580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763973580" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763973580?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763973580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4308704236252304778">I read this book as some light reading in between. For some fluff. Imagine my surprise when I found that what was between the pages was instead a profound quest for the meaning of life and love; a story of self-discovery and humour beyond measure.<br/><br/>The chapters were written by two different authors - Rachel Cohn writing Lily's and David Levithan writing Dash's. Apparently (according to the information at the end of the book) they swapped chapters much like Dash and Lily swapped dares. And it works</span>
  <span id="freeText4308704236252304778" style="display:none">I read this book as some light reading in between. For some fluff. Imagine my surprise when I found that what was between the pages was instead a profound quest for the meaning of life and love; a story of self-discovery and humour beyond measure.<br /><br />The chapters were written by two different authors - Rachel Cohn writing Lily's and David Levithan writing Dash's. Apparently (according to the information at the end of the book) they swapped chapters much like Dash and Lily swapped dares. And it works perfectly.<br /><br />What struck me most was how much many of Dash's and Lily's views resonated with me. Just to give you a glimpse, here's a notebook entry from Dash:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>We believe the wrong things. […] That’s what frustrates me the most. Not the lack of belief, but the belief in the wrong things. You want meaning? Well, the meanings are out there. We’re just so damn good at reading them wrong. […] I don’t think meaning is something that can be explained. You have to understand it on your own. It’s like when you’re starting to read. First, you learn the letters. Then, once you know what sounds the letters make, you use them to sound out words. You know that c-a-t leads to cat and d-o-g leads to dog. But then you have to make that extra leap, to understand that the word, the sond, the „cat“ is connected to an actual cat, and that „dog“ is connected to an actual dog. It’s that leap, that understanding, that leads to meaning. And a lot of the time in life, we’re still just sounding things out. We know the sentences and how to say them. We know the ideas and how to present them. We know the prayers and which words to say in what order. But that’s only spelling.</i>
</blockquote><br />Or here a notebook entry from Lily:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I want to belive there is a somebody out there just for me. I want to believe that I exist to be there for that somebody.</i>
</blockquote><br />Some musing from Lily's brother Langston:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>The important people in our lives leave imprints. They may stay or go in the physical realm, but they are always there in your heart, because they helped form your heart. There’s no getting over that.</i>
</blockquote><br />And some wisdom from Sofia:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>It’s up to you, not fate.</i>
</blockquote><br />You see what I mean, then, about this book being profound? Elemental questions asked and answered by not just Dash and Lily but, to some extend, the people around them (young and old). <br /><br />Not to mention the refreshingly natural way the authors included people from the LGBTQ community without seeming pretentious or forcing the issue to be up-to-date (I hate that so much in most currently released stories).<br /><br />But there were two negative points too. <br />Maybe it's because I was always a pretty sincere person (joking around, sure, but I mean when it comes to the cornerstones of life), even at the age of 16, that I did not like/support the prospect of "let's see where this takes us". I mean, Dash basically told Lily that he'd be with Sofia if she wasn't living in Spain, that Lily therefore is sort of a consolation prize! <br />Many people will forgive this, also because most people believe in "just being with someone you like" and "getting experienced" or "enjoying love whenever it comes your way" whereas silly little me actually believes in The One. <br />Others might also forgive this because the MCs are only 16. But as I said, I was like that even back then (which explains a lot). And for such "frivolity" to come from Dash of all people, who has been through a rough divorce/custody battle so he knows how love can hurt and shouldn't be handed out to just anybody ... <br />And then there was Lily's night of "fun" that wasn't much better. <br />I'm not saying these two things were portrayed in an unrealistic way, just that I don't like it (neither in real life nor in stories).<br /><br />The rest was, of course, pretty sweet. Poetic and nerdy and (thanks to Lily's extended family as well as some overbearing mothers and a dog named Boris) ludicruously funny. So yes, I enjoyed the hell out of it, not least because both MCs are pretty bookish so that was something else I could identify with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4308704236252304778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_624035131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624035131" />
    <a title="Hershey " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19468761-hershey"><img alt="Hershey " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599546236p2/19468761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624035131?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hershey " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hershey " href="/user/show/19468761-hershey">Hershey </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375859557" href="/book/show/10264464-dash-lily-s-book-of-dares">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624035131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12050577516869632621">Oh dear.<br/><br/>I was so prepared to fall for this book.<br/><br/>I was expecting something <b>quirky, fun and extremely cute.</b> I was expecting this book to put me in a festive mood even though Christmas is still months away. I just wanted something refreshing. <b>I wanted something like hot chocolate and marshmallows and snow!</b> Yeah, I'm kind of in that mood right now.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403437291ra/10093409.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>See those lights? I thought this book was like those lights, fun and changing and just awesome.<br/><br/>I didn't get any of that. I didn't even feel anything other</span>
  <span id="freeText12050577516869632621" style="display:none">Oh dear.<br><br>I was so prepared to fall for this book.<br><br>I was expecting something <b>quirky, fun and extremely cute.</b> I was expecting this book to put me in a festive mood even though Christmas is still months away. I just wanted something refreshing. <b>I wanted something like hot chocolate and marshmallows and snow!</b> Yeah, I'm kind of in that mood right now.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403437291ra/10093409.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>See those lights? I thought this book was like those lights, fun and changing and just awesome.<br><br>I didn't get any of that. I didn't even feel anything other than the need to finish this book soon so that I can move on to the next one.<br><br>What I did get were <b>two annoying, pretentious main characters who irked me like crazy.</b> Dash and Lily were constantly trying to be smart and snarly and cool. They didn't seem like realistic characters to me. You know that feeling you get when you see someone trying to act really smart and cool and completely failing at it? I had that feeling throughout the whole book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403437291i/10093410.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12050577516869632621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m9PQHLrJnnT0Nc3IeewCFCSDHjCJvk99jbforjsS8VoKBPd5m++p5dpCF/NXpwH1GAq0qCP0Y6cMgz73xrA8PA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4iRAJcv/qbS3X1sCRh6kAnUrPgmSxCogm5NGb4EMLZBz82dA6tmeJZkogTloVafjSaKUkTiOBvoap5A2fK7g9g==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer16630864863902133151">Rachel grew up in the D.C. area and graduated from Barnard College with a B.A. in Political Science. She has written many YA novels, including three that she cowrote with her friend and colleague <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' title='David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a>. She lives and writes (when she's not reading other people's books, organizing her music library or looking for the best cappuccino) in New York City.</span>
